# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes API Server Admission Controller Chain

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement the API server admission controller pipeline: the admission.Interface registration, the generic admission chain execution, the mutating admission ordering, and the validating admission webhook call.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the platform domain.

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

## API Server Admission Controller Pipeline Files

I identified **12 key Go source files** in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement the API server admission controller pipeline:

### Core Components:

1. **admission.Interface Definition** - `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/interfaces.go`
   - Defines `Interface`, `MutationInterface`, and `ValidationInterface`
   - Core types for all admission plugins

2. **Generic Admission Chain** - `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/chain.go`
   - `chainAdmissionHandler` iterates through plugins
   - `Admit()` and `Validate()` methods execute the chain sequentially

3. **Plugin Registry & Chain Building** - `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugins.go`
   - `Plugins` type manages plugin factories
   - `NewFromPlugins()` builds the admission chain by loading plugins in order

4. **Re-invocation Handler** - `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/reinvocation.go`
   - Wraps chain to re-invoke mutating plugins if mutations occur

5. **Admission Ordering** - `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/admission.go`
   - `AdmissionOptions` defines `RecommendedPluginOrder`
   - Ensures mutating plugins run before validating ones
   - `ApplyTo()` applies the chain to server config

6. **Mutating Webhook Plugin** - `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/mutating/plugin.go`
   - Implements `MutationInterface`

7. **Mutating Webhook Dispatcher** - `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/mutating/dispatcher.go`
   - Calls mutating webhooks sequentially with patch application

When trying to overwrite annotation with a new value, an error is returned.\n65: \t// Both ValidationInterface and MutationInterface are allowed to add Annotations.\n66: \t// By default, an annotation gets logged into audit event if the request's audit level is greater or\n67: \t// equal to Metadata.\n68: \tAddAnnotation(key, value string) error\n69: \n70: \t// AddAnnotationWithLevel sets annotation according to key-value pair with additional intended audit level.\n71: \t// An Annotation gets logged into audit event if the request's audit level is greater or equal to the\n72: \t// intended audit level.\n73: \tAddAnnotationWithLevel(key, value string, level auditinternal.Level) error\n74: \n75: \t// GetReinvocationContext tracks the admission request information relevant to the re-invocation policy.\n76: \tGetReinvocationContext() ReinvocationContext\n77: }\n78: \n79: // ObjectInterfaces is an interface used by AdmissionController to get object interfaces\n80: // such as Converter or Defaulter. These interfaces are normally coming from Request Scope\n81: // to handle special cases like CRDs.\n82: type ObjectInterfaces interface {\n83: \t// GetObjectCreater is the ObjectCreator appropriate for the requested object.\n84: \tGetObjectCreater() runtime.ObjectCreater\n85: \t// GetObjectTyper is the ObjectTyper appropriate for the requested object.\n86: \tGetObjectTyper() runtime.ObjectTyper\n87: \t// GetObjectDefaulter is the ObjectDefaulter appropriate for the requested object.\n88: \tGetObjectDefaulter() runtime.ObjectDefaulter\n89: \t// GetObjectConvertor is the ObjectConvertor appropriate for the requested object.\n90: \tGetObjectConvertor() runtime.ObjectConvertor\n91: \t// GetEquivalentResourceMapper is the EquivalentResourceMapper appropriate for finding equivalent resources and expected kind for the requested object.\n92: \tGetEquivalentResourceMapper() runtime.EquivalentResourceMapper\n93: }\n94: \n95: // privateAnnotationsGetter is a private interface which allows users to get annotations from Attributes.\n96: type privateAnnotationsGetter interface {\n97: \tgetAnnotations(maxLevel auditinternal.Level) map[string]string\n98: }\n99: \n100: // AnnotationsGetter allows users to get annotations from Attributes. An alternate Attribute should implement\n101: // this interface.\n102: type AnnotationsGetter interface {\n103: \tGetAnnotations(maxLevel auditinternal.Level) map[string]string\n104: }\n105: \n106: // ReinvocationContext provides access to the admission related state required to implement the re-invocation policy.\n107: type ReinvocationContext interface {\n108: \t// IsReinvoke returns true if the current admission check is a re-invocation.\n109: \tIsReinvoke() bool\n110: \t// SetIsReinvoke sets the current admission check as a re-invocation.\n111: \tSetIsReinvoke()\n112: \t// ShouldReinvoke returns true if any plugin has requested a re-invocation.\n113: \tShouldReinvoke() bool\n114: \t// SetShouldReinvoke signals that a re-invocation is desired.\n115: \tSetShouldReinvoke()\n116: \t// AddValue set a value for a plugin name, possibly overriding a previous value.\n117: \tSetValue(plugin string, v interface{})\n118: \t// Value reads a value for a webhook.\n119: \tValue(plugin string) interface{}\n120: }\n121: \n122: // Interface is an abstract, pluggable interface for Admission Control decisions.\n123: type Interface interface {\n124: \t// Handles returns true if this admission controller can handle the given operation\n125: \t// where operation can be one of CREATE, UPDATE, DELETE, or CONNECT\n126: \tHandles(operation Operation) bool\n127: }\n128: \n129: type MutationInterface interface {\n130: \tInterface\n131: \n132: \t// Admit makes an admission decision based on the request attributes.\n133: \t// Context is used only for timeout/deadline/cancellation and tracing information.\n134: \tAdmit(ctx context.Context, a Attributes, o ObjectInterfaces) (err error)\n135: }\n136: \n137: // ValidationInterface is an abstract, pluggable interface for Admission Control decisions.\n138: type ValidationInterface interface {\n139: \tInterface\n140: \n141: \t// Validate makes an admission decision based on the request attributes.  It is NOT allowed to mutate\n142: \t// Context is used only for timeout/deadline/cancellation and tracing information.\n143: \tValidate(ctx context.Context, a Attributes, o ObjectInterfaces) (err error)\n144: }\n145: \n146: // Operation is the type of resource operation being checked for admission control\n147: type Operation string\n148: \n149: // Operation constants\n150: const (\n151: \tCreate  Operation = \"CREATE\"\n152: \tUpdate  Operation = \"UPDATE\"\n153: \tDelete  Operation = \"DELETE\"\n154: \tConnect Operation = \"CONNECT\"\n155: )\n156: \n157: // PluginInitializer is used for initialization of shareable resources between admission plugins.\n158: // After initialization the resources have to be set separately\n159: type PluginInitializer interface {\n160: \tInitialize(plugin Interface)\n161: }\n162: \n163: // InitializationValidator holds ValidateInitialization functions, which are responsible for validation of initialized\n164: // shared resources and should be implemented on admission plugins\n165: type InitializationValidator interface {\n166: \tValidateInitialization() error\n167: }\n168: \n169: // ConfigProvider provides a way to get configuration for an admission plugin based on its name\n170: type ConfigProvider interface {\n171: \tConfigFor(pluginName string) (io.Reader, error)\n172: }\n173: ",

The architecture consists of:\\n\\n1. **Core Interfaces (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/interfaces.go)**: Defines the fundamental `Interface` type that all admission plugins must implement, with `MutationInterface` for mutating admission (implementing `Admit()`) and `ValidationInterface` for validating admission (implementing `Validate()`). The `Attributes` interface provides metadata about requests being admitted.\\n\\n2. **Generic Admission Chain (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/chain.go)**: Implements `chainAdmissionHandler` which iterates through multiple admission plugins sequentially. The `Admit()` method processes mutating plugins in order, stopping on first error. The `Validate()` method processes validating plugins similarly. Both methods check plugin registration via `Handles()` before calling.\\n\\n3. **Plugin Registry and Chain Building (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugins.go)**: The `Plugins` registry stores factory functions for each plugin. The critical `NewFromPlugins()` method creates the admission chain by:\\n   - Loading each plugin from the registry\\n   - Initializing plugins with context via `PluginInitializer`\\n   - Tracking which are `MutationInterface` vs `ValidationInterface`\\n   - Wrapping with decorators (e.g., metrics)\\n   - Returning a `reinvocationHandler` wrapping the chain\\n\\n4. **Plugin Registration (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/plugins.go)**: `RegisterAllAdmissionPlugins()` registers the default plugins including `lifecycle`, `validatingwebhook`, `mutatingwebhook`, `validatingadmissionpolicy`, and `mutatingadmissionpolicy`.\\n\\n5. **Mutating Admission Ordering (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/admission.go)**: `AdmissionOptions` defines the `RecommendedPluginOrder` which ensures mutating plugins execute before validating ones. The `ApplyTo()` method applies the admission chain to server configuration, calling `NewFromPlugins()` to build the chain with enabled plugins in the recommended order.\\n\\n6. **Mutating Webhook Plugin (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/mutating/plugin.go)**: Implements `Plugin` as a `MutationInterface`. The `Admit()` method delegates to `Webhook.Dispatch()`.\\n\\n7. **Mutating Webhook Dispatcher (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/mutating/dispatcher.go)**: Iterates through registered mutating webhooks, calling each via REST. The `Dispatch()` method handles re-invocation context, applies JSON patches from webhook responses, and tracks mutations for audit annotations.\\n\\n8. **Validating Webhook Plugin (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/validating/plugin.go)**: Implements `Plugin` as a `ValidationInterface`. The `Validate()` method delegates to `Webhook.Dispatch()`.\\n\\n9. **Validating Webhook Dispatcher (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/validating/dispatcher.go)**: Calls validating webhooks in parallel using goroutines. The `Dispatch()` method constructs versioned attributes, evaluates match conditions, and returns on first error.\\n\\n10. **Generic Webhook Infrastructure (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/generic/webhook.go)**: Provides shared `Webhook` struct used by both mutating and validating plugins. The `Dispatch()` method calls `dispatcher.Dispatch()` after validating readiness. The `ShouldCallHook()` method evaluates namespace selectors, object selectors, rules, and match conditions to determine if a webhook should be invoked.\\n\\n11. **Re-invocation Handler (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/reinvocation.go)**: The `reinvoker` wraps the admission chain and implements re-invocation logic. After initial `Admit()`, if `ReinvocationContext.ShouldReinvoke()` is true (indicating mutations occurred), it calls `Admit()` again, allowing eligible webhooks to reinvoke.\\n\\n12. **Metrics (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/metrics/metrics.go)**: Decorators wrap plugins to emit admission metrics. The `WithStepMetrics()` decorator tracks admission timing and rejection reasons separately for mutating and validating phases.\\n\\nThe execution flow: API request \u2192 `Server.Config.AdmissionControl.Admit()` \u2192 reinvoker \u2192 chainAdmissionHandler \u2192 each mutating plugin in order \u2192 reinvoker re-invokes if needed \u2192 chainAdmissionHandler \u2192 each validating plugin (webhooks in parallel) \u2192 response allowed/rejected.\"\n}\n",
